{1}}There are lots of programming tasks that deal with generating
    reports in the tabular format. Usually such documents should be designed
    for reviewing by people who are not closely familiar with different
    technologies and prefer to obtain reports in a usual format. For Microsoft
    Windows users, the most common office solution is Microsoft Office, and
    when talking about electronic worksheets, it is undoubtedly Microsoft
    Excel.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%

{5.5\p@}\def\saMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\saConditional%
{1}}The JExcel library allows Java programmers for Windows to easily
    create, modify or display Microsoft Excel files. Using this library, you
    can work with workbook files, print a workbook, worksheet or even a
    specific range of cells, and modify cell values, cell number formats, etc.
    Also, there is an ability to customize cell appearance, including text
    font, cell background and border, text alignment and orientation,
    etc.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}JExcel can be used for solving different tasks from simple display
    of a workbook in a standalone Excel application to handling Excel events
    and embedding a workbook into Java Swing applications. The use of the
    library is very simple and doesn't require from a Java programmer specific
    knowledge of Microsoft Office programming.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}Excel sends notifications about its various events. JExcel provides
    the \Node%

    \Node%

    \Node%

{1}}Excel also generate some controlled events that can affect a
    workbook or worksheet behavior. Note that listeners and adapters allow you
    just to obtain notifications. To hande such events, there are also the
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{220}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}WorkbookEventHandler\endSeq{}\endNode{} and
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{221}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}WorksheetEventHandler\endSeq{}\endNode{} interfaces provided. A
    notification about a controlled event is sent to event listeners
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{222}}\Seq%
{\def\fPosture%
{italic}}after\endSeq{}\endNode{} it is processed by a handler, because the
    handler can forbid processing the event and in this case listeners don't
    obtain the notification. Instances of \Node%
{\def\Element%
{223}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Application\endSeq{}\endNode{},
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{224}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Workbook\endSeq{}\endNode{} and \Node%
{\def\Element%
{225}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Worksheet\endSeq{}\endNode{} can
    have several listeners, however each instance cannot have more than one
    event handler.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{9.9\p@}}WorksheetEventHandler.beforeRightClick()\endSeq{}\endNode{}
        method is called when the user right-\/clicks in a worksheet, but before
        processing the event. The handler can forbid the event processing by
        returning \Node%

{336}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fPosture%
{italic}}false\endSeq{}\endNode{}. In this case neither listeners
        will obtain the notification, nor Excel will process the event (Excel
        usually shows a pop-\/up menu). Return \Node%

        allow processing the right-\/click event.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}~~~~~~~~worksheet.setEventHandler(new~WorksheetEventHandler()
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~public~boolean~beforeDoubleClick(WorksheetEventObject~eventObject)
~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~//Forbid~double-\/clicking~on~"A1"~cell
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~if~(eventObject.getCell().equals(eventObject.getWorksheet().getCell("A1")))
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~return~false;
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~else
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~return~true;
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~~~~~\}

~~~~~~~~~~~~public~boolean~beforeRightClick(WorksheetEventObject~eventObject)
~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~//Allow~right-\/clicking~only~on~"A1"~cell
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~if~(eventObject.getRange().equals(eventObject.getWorksheet().getRange("A1")))
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~return~true;
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~else
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~return~false;
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~~~~~\}

{\def\Element%
{432}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Range\endSeq{}\endNode{} class for working
      with ranges of cells. To obtain an instance of the
      \Node%
{\def\Element%
{433}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Range\endSeq{}\endNode{} class, the \Node%
{\def\Element%
{434}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Worksheet\endSeq{}\endNode{}
      class has the \Node%
{\def\Element%
{435}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Workbook.getRange()\endSeq{}\endNode{} method. This
      method takes a string representation of a necessary range of cells in
      any format supported by Excel. Despite this fact, it is recommended to
      refer to only simple ranges like "A1:V1" or "B23:AA45" and avoid
      referencing a range like "A1:B4;A7;D12:G45", because compound ranges use
      a separator (in the example it is the ';' symbol) which differs
      depending on Excel settings. So an application that uses compound range
      references may work incorrectly if Excel has another separator
      settings.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%

{1}}The sample below demonstrates the technique of searching for
      values of different types:\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%
{515}}\Par%
{\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}\def\LineSpacing%
{10.89\p@}\def\LineSpacingFactor%

{11\p@}\def\saConditional%
{1}}~~~~~~~~//Getting~a~necessary~range
~~~~~~~~Range~range~=~worksheet.getRange("A1:C5").include("D1");

~~~~~~~~//Specifying~search~attributes
~~~~~~~~Range.SearchAttributes~searchAttributes~=~new~Range.SearchAttributes();
~~~~~~~~searchAttributes.setCaseSensetive(true);
~~~~~~~~searchAttributes.setLookIn(Range.FindLookIn.VALUES);
~~~~~~~~searchAttributes.setForwardDirection(true);

~~~~~~~~//Looking~for~a~string~value
~~~~~~~~String~strValue~=~"Grapefruit";
~~~~~~~~Cell~cell~=~range.find(strValue,~searchAttributes);
~~~~~~~~if~(cell~==~null)
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println("\char92{}""~+~strValue~+~"\char92{}"~was~not~found.");
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~else
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println("\char92{}""~+~strValue~+~"\char92{}"~was~found~in~"~+~cell.getAddress());
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~cell~=~range.findNext();
~~~~~~~~if~(cell~==~null)
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println("\char92{}""~+~strValue~+~"\char92{}"~was~not~found.");
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~else
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println("\char92{}""~+~strValue~+~"\char92{}"~was~found~in~"~+~cell.getAddress());
~~~~~~~~\}

~~~~~~~~//Looking~for~a~long~calculated~value
~~~~~~~~long~longValue~=~39;
~~~~~~~~cell~=~range.find(longValue,~searchAttributes);
~~~~~~~~if~(cell~==~null)
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println(longValue~+~"~was~not~found.");
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~else
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~System.out.println(longValue~+~"~was~found~in~"~+~cell.getAddress());
~~~~~~~~\}\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}JExcel provides functionality for sorting rows or columns in a
      range of cells. For this purpose, use the
      \Node%
{\def\Element%
{523}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Range.sort()\endSeq{}\endNode{} method. It takes a column name
      (for example, "A", "D", "AB") for sorting rows by the values of the
      specified column and a row number (for example, 1, 4, 100) for sorting
      columns by the values of the specified row.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

      \Node%

      (or \Node%

      \Node%

      \Node%

      \Node%

{1}}If you try to iterate over cells in range to read cell values the
      performance will be extremely low. Such result is predictable because
      each cell reading operation produces several COM interface related Java
      objects, which allocate some physical memory and will not be immediately
      removed from memory after interface call. Large numbers of the objects
      can result out of memory. To avoid it and improve reading performance
      you can use \Node%

{1}}The range number format reflects the way of displaying numeric
      data. For instance, a double value can be represented as an integer or
      as a date. A number format in Excel is set by a string pattern in a
      specific locale-\/dependent format. For detailed specification of the
      number format, please refer to appropriate articles on Excel.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}~~~~~~~~//Creating~a~new~instance~of~the~com.jniwrapper.win32.jexcel.Font~class
~~~~~~~~Font~font~=~new~Font();

~~~~~~~~//Changing~font~name
~~~~~~~~font.setName("Courier~New");

~~~~~~~~//Changing~font~styles
~~~~~~~~font.setBold(true);
~~~~~~~~font.setStrikethrough(true);
~~~~~~~~font.setUnderlineStyle(Font.UnderlineStyle.DOUBLE);

~~~~~~~~//Applying~new~font~setting

{1}}~~~~public~String~getAlignmentAsString(Font.Alignment~alignment)
~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~if~(alignment.equals(Font.Alignment.SUBSCRIPT))
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~return~"Subscript";
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~~~else~if~(alignment.equals(Font.Alignment.SUPERSCRIPT))
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~return~"Superscript";
~~~~~~~~\}

~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~return~"Normal";

{1}}To customize a range or cell border, you need to specify the kind
      of border to work with. There are several standard kinds of borders
      which are provided in JExcel as instances of the
      \Node%
{\def\Element%
{746}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border.Kind\endSeq{}\endNode{} class. For example,
      \Node%
{\def\Element%
{747}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border.Kind.EDGELEFT\endSeq{}\endNode{} or
      \Node%
{\def\Element%
{748}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border.Kind.EDGETOP\endSeq{}\endNode{}.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{749}}\Par%

{\def\Element%
{750}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%

      to obtain an instance of the \Node%
{\def\Element%
{751}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border\endSeq{}\endNode{} class that
      corresponds to some border kind. The \Node%
{\def\Element%
{752}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border\endSeq{}\endNode{} class
      resides in the \Node%
{\def\Element%
{753}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}com.jniwrapper.win32.jexcel\endSeq{}\endNode{}
      package.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

      set using the constants from the \Node%

      \Node%

{758}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}LineStyle.DASHDOT\endSeq{}\endNode{}, etc. The line weight is set
      using the constants from the \Node%
{\def\Element%
{759}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Border.LineWeight\endSeq{}\endNode{}
      class: \Node%

      \Node%

{1}}~~~~~~~~//Getting~the~top~border
~~~~~~~~Border~topBorder~=~range.getBorder(Border.Kind.EDGETOP);

~~~~~~~~//Getting~the~border~style
~~~~~~~~java.awt.Color~borderColor~=~topBorder.getColor();
~~~~~~~~Border.LineStyle~lineStyle~=~topBorder.getLineStyle();
~~~~~~~~Border.LineWeight~lineWeight~=~topBorder.getWeight();

~~~~~~~~//Setting~new~border~style
~~~~~~~~Border~border~=~new~Border();
~~~~~~~~border.setColor(Color.CYAN);
~~~~~~~~border.setLineStyle(Border.LineStyle.DASHDOT);
~~~~~~~~border.setWeight(Border.LineWeight.MEDIUM);

~~~~~~~~//Applying~the~border~settings~to~the~top~border
~~~~~~~~range.setBorder(Border.Kind.EDGETOP,~border);\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

      \Node%

{1}}Since JExcel ver.1.4 JWorkbook allows creating multiple embedded
      MS Excel workbook instances in Swing applications. These instances are
      connected to common MS Excel process. Such feature allows implementing
      MDI applications and provides more flexible way for MS Excel documents
      processing.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{\def\Element%
{839}\def\ProcessingMode%
{title-sosofo-mode}}JWorkbook objects handling on application exit\endNode{}\def\HeadingText{%
10.6. JWorkbook objects handling on application exit}%
\endHeadPar{}\endSeq{}\Node%
{\def\Element%
{839}}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%
{840}}\Par%
{\def\FirstLineStartIndent%
{0\p@}\def\FirstLineStartIndentFactor%
{0}\def\Quadding%
{justify}\def\Hyphenate%
{0}\def\Language%
{EN}\def\sbNom%
{5.5\p@}\def\sbMin%
{5.5\p@}\def\sbMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\sbConditional%
{1}\def\saNom%
{5.5\p@}\def\saMin%
{5.5\p@}\def\saMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\saConditional%
{1}}If you are using JWorkbook objects in different JFrames you need
      correctly handling application exit closing all JWorkbook instances.
      This issue is due by JWorkbook native resource releasing requirement.
      When you close the main window using EXIT\char95{}ON\char95{}CLOSE flag, JVM doesn't
      send the corresponding window close event to all opened JFrames and
      JWorkbook objects cannot be released automatically. Therefore in such
      case JWorkbook related application produces exception on exit and hangs
      up EXCEL process.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%
{841}}\Par%
{\def\FirstLineStartIndent%

{5.5\p@}\def\sbMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\sbConditional%
{1}\def\saNom%
{5.5\p@}\def\saMin%
{5.5\p@}\def\saMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\saConditional%
{1}}To avoid such issue, you need to call JWorkbook close() method for
      all JWorkbook objects on application exit:\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%

{1}}private~java.util.List~jworkbookList~=~new~LinkedList();

...

//Add~all~JWorkbook~references~to~jworkbookList
JWorkbook~jworkbook~=~new~JWorkbook();
jworkbookList.add(jworkbook);

...

//On~application~window~close~correctly~release~JWorkbook~objects
frame.addWindowListener(new~WindowAdapter()
\{
~~~~public~void~windowClosing(WindowEvent~e)
~~~~\{
~~~~~~while~(!jworkbookList.isEmpty())
~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~JWorkbook~jworkbook~=~(JWorkbook)~jworkbookList.remove(0);
~~~~~~~~if~(jworkbook~!=~null~\&\&~!jworkbook.isClosed())
~~~~~~~~\{
~~~~~~~~~~~~jworkbook.close();
~~~~~~~~\}
~~~~~~\}
~~~~\}

{1}}JExcel provides peers for the following classes:
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{848}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Application\endSeq{}\endNode{}, \Node%
{\def\Element%
{849}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Workbook\endSeq{}\endNode{},
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{850}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Worksheet\endSeq{}\endNode{}, \Node%
{\def\Element%
{851}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Range\endSeq{}\endNode{}, and
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{852}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Cell\endSeq{}\endNode{}. The peers can be useful for implementation of
    Excel functions that are not available in the current version of JExcel.
    Excel controls are not thread-\/safe, therefore their functions should be
    called from the same thread. For the JExcel library, it is the OLE message
    loop. This is important when you are working with native peer objects,
    namely when calling methods and querying the interface.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
{\def\Element%
{853}}\Par%
{\def\FirstLineStartIndent%

{5.5\p@}\def\saMax%
{5.5\p@}\def\saConditional%
{1}}The following sample demonstrates the correct usage of the
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{854}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Application\endSeq{}\endNode{} native peer and the OLE message
    loop:\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%

{1}}The \Node%
{\def\Element%
{857}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}OleMessageLoop\endSeq{}\endNode{} class provides two methods
    for executing methods in this thread:
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{858}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}doInvokeLater()\endSeq{}\endNode{} and
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{859}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}doInvokeAndWait()\endSeq{}\endNode{}. The difference between them is
    that the former returns immediately, and the latter blocks further
    execution while the task defined by \Node%
{\def\Element%
{860}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}Runnable\endSeq{}\endNode{}
    method parameter is being executed. Use the
    \Node%
{\def\Element%
{861}}\Seq%
{\def\fFamName{Palatino}\def\fSize%
{9.9\p@}}doInvokeLater()\endSeq{}\endNode{} method in a Swing thread for
    time-\/consuming tasks to prevent this thread from blocking.\endPar{}\endNode{}\Node%
